This place is really good!
They have very good furniture options for a lot of tastes but obviously does the mod look mostly. My partner and I have been couch shopping for a month now and decided to check this place out based on the reviews of the quality they sell. Once in the store it was awesome. One of the things I hated shopping at other places is the employees following us around answering questions we did not ask and constantly placing themselves in our discussion as we talked with ourselves about our purchase.

We get our couch this Friday! I'll post in the next few months but I'm sure we are going to love it! The quality in store was phenomenal< /review>

< review>
Wonderful experience.

I needed to print out a name badge for a Halloween costume.  First I went to FedEx Print center.  I am told to get on a self service computer (at .30 a minute) and bring up the attachment in MS Paint, where I can print it for over $1, but of course it is the wrong size, and I cant figure out how to get it to print in actual size, then I have to figure out how to re-scale the thing and end up pissed off and frustrated and walking out of the place in disgust after spending over $10 without even getting what I wanted yet.

I then went down to Mr. Kopy.

"Oh sure, just email us the attachment, we will scale it, print it, and  laminate it for you"

I come back 30 minutes later, they charge me $4 for exactly what I wanted, that is half the price I paid to FedEx, and I got exactly what I came in wanting.

There is no comparison.  Don't waste your time down at FedEx, just come downtown and these guys will take care of you.< /review>

< userid>
110154708357398947388</userid>
<Name>Dan Seguin</Name>< Time>
1468296495057< /Time>
< Rating>
4</Rating>
< Text>
Had my dog with me and some time to kill while waiting to give a ride to a friend, so thought I'd do some some exploring. Saw the sign and entered a rather unassuming parking lot with no expectations. Both dog and I ended up really enjoying ourselves. Just past the small rectangular lot with parking and concrete picnic tables on one side, a sandy trail snaked through some low brush and through a cut in the small hill to reveal several rows of  20-40' sand  dunes dotted with clusters of brush as far as the eye could see in one direction, and perhaps 3-4 large dunes and valleys between the trailhead and the beach (which I never made it too). Instead I climbed the sliding face of one of the closest tallest dunes (not easy) and rested under a wind-swept tree along it's winding peak. It was a very bizarre sight, one side of this mount was pristine white sand and scrub, but the backside descended into a loamy, shady, forested area, that descended another 40' below the dune's base down to a set of trails that cris-crossed a dry stream bed. Time was up for exploring, but I'll definitely be back, next time allotting more exploration time. Lastly, you might think an area like that with it's many private hidden spots might be populated with transients and littered with trash, but none of either was to be seen. A potential nice place to get away with someone for an afternoon and find a fun spot to relax.</Text>

<response>None< /response><time>1365477725532< /time><username>Alex Yamada<//username><UserId.>116066068635808570421<//UserId.><Text>I've found myself with a serious craving for a nice big bowl of pho lately, so I decided to head down from Marysville to give this place a go.  Now, I'm a bit of a purist when it comes to pho.  I don't like anything fancy or new-fangled; just a traditional steaming bowl of well-made broth, simple rice noodles, a good helping of the appropriate cuts of beef and a plate of fresh herbs and bean sprouts to compliment them.  Hit all these marks, and you've won a permanent place in my heart.  Here's how "Pho Saigon's" house special fared on all of these points:

The Broth- Honestly, the broth was disappointing.  It lacked the depth of spice that is the hallmark of carefully made, good pho broth.  Traditional spices such as star anise and roasted ginger were nearly imperceptible and the resulting liquid was more akin to warm, beefy saltwater.  By no means was it bad or unpalatable, merely disappointing when you've had the truly good stuff before.

The Noodles- Let's face it, it's pretty darn hard to mess up rice noodles.  Save for when they're severely undercooked and still brittle or overcooked and mushy, rice noodles are pretty generically rice noodles.  These were cooked appropriately and, of all the factors I look for in good pho, the only one I have no complaints about.

The Meat- My favorite part of pho is by far and wide the meat.  Thinly sliced cuts of rare beef flank, Vietnamese-style meatballs and an assortment of cuts that are usually seen as undesirable in American cuisine (tripe, tendons and other fatty or cartilaginous bits and pieces) become pure heaven when slowly simmered in a good broth.  The meat at "Pho Saigon" was actually quite good, but the quantity was a major disappointment.  I requested (for an additional $2) extra meat to be put in my soup, but what I was given hardly amounted to what I would receive at my usual pho joints without requesting extra.  This was extremely obvious when I realized that when it came to the Vietnamese meatballs, I had only been given half of one.  Skimp on the noodles if you must, but go cheap on the meat and you've lost me.

The Herb Plate- Pretty much standard to nearly all pho restaurants is the plate of herbs and bean sprouts that accompany your food.  "Pho Saigon" was no different.  This one consisted of a bed of fresh bean sprouts, two slices of raw jalapeno, a branch of none-to-fresh Thai basil that had been harvested far too late and half of a lemon wedge.  Again, they seemed to skimp in one of the key aspects of pho.  Aside from the overly mature basil being more bitter than fragrant, I had expected to have a choice between lemon and lime (and certainly more than half a wedge).

For all of their shortcomings in terms of food quality, the waitress was extremely courteous and provided very good service throughout the entire meal.  The decor was simple and neat and provided a fairly uninteresting but pleasant eating environment.  All in all, "Pho Saigon" was worth the $10 for a large-sized bowl (though I have had better for less), but not the 45-minute drive.  I may or may not return to this restaurant in the future.  It's one of those take it or leave it situations.</Text>< pictures>

<Review>I lived in Hollywood for 20 years and this was probably my favorite restaurant in the area. Not only is the food amazing, but they had two things that were super rare for any restaurant in Hollywood: ample parking, and rarely any kind of wait for a table. Maybe it's because many people don't know about it or don't consider it a place to dine in? Their takeout is also amazing, which is great now during the pandemic, as that's all they're offering. This place is magnificent. Highly recommended for anyone who appreciates a good Jewish deli, although they also have great non-deli food (like Thanksgiving dinner every day of the year, and Italian dishes, etc). Even though I don't live in Hollywood any more, I always make a point of going back whenever I can, even though it's over an hour round trip for me to go nowadays. Give this place a shot, you won't regret it.</Review>< Pics>

<UserId.>107536141480438482815<//UserId.><Pics>None</Pics>< Text>
This is one of my VERY FAVORITE restaurants, EVER! The beef brisket is beyond words... but let me try: you wont find a better, more perfectly delicious brisket sandwich anywhere else. Period. I have mine on egg bread with multiple slices of swiss cheese and I dip it into a hot dish of au jus. It is just perfection. I get a side of macaroni salad, again perfection. I wash this down with Dr. Browns root beer or dark cherry soda. Then for a taste of something sweet I have a slice of their magnificent New York cheesecake. I don't care for cheesecake with grahamcracker crust and that is why I love the cheesecake at Greenblatts so much: it has sort of a sugar cookie type crust which is so much more lovely with the velvety cheese filling. It is a tall cheesecake with a generous amount of cheese filling- not too sweet, not too sour. I dream about it often. I have been a Greenblatts customer since 1978 when the first began delivering lunch to my first apartment in West Hollywood. There is a good reason why this famous Jewish deli has thrived for all these years. Everything on their menu is the highest quality available and is as fresh as can be. See for yourself why this restaurant has such an excellent reputation.<//Text>

Incredibly disappointed by Greenblatt's Deli.  I've been going here and ordering from the for years and I'm sad to say they've gone downhill.

Today, I placed an order by phone for delivery at 4:20PM and they told me it could be up to 90-minutes, which I was OK with.  I called them after they didn't show up during the delivery time window, and they were completely unapologetic, and accused me of lying about the delivery window.  Luckily they were on speaker when I placed the order and my partner heard. They informed me that the driver left their place at 4PM and had 5 deliveries. By this time, my sandwich would have been sitting around, getting soggy for over an hour, and my soup would have been lukewarm at best. I told them my concern and they didn't care and offered no other options to make me happy, so I cancelled the order.

Just last month, the owner of the shop was talking to me about how they're struggling- and with service like this, I can see why.

I will update my post if they ever reach out to me.</review>

< Review>
Come here for the food, although they have a good wine selection. Easily the best pastrami in the area. I prefer theirs over Langer's.
They use bread from La Brea bakery for their sandwiches. You can also be order their meats by itself from the counter, along with other items.
I love their kreplach soup. I've had their French Dip sandwich and would pass on this, as the au jus was too salty. Their tuna sandwich is delicious and if you like corned beef, they have really good corned beef. Their sides could use some work, but I'm fine with that.</Review>

< Text>
I love this deli's location (next to the Laugh Factory) & its hours.  Reading the book "Save the Deli" by David Sax inspired me to try the pastrami sandwich here w/ a glass of Pinot Noir from Ojai.  The waitress helped me select that particular varietal.  I had half a pastrami sandwich w/ russian dressing, cheese, & cole slaw.  I also had a cup of matzo ball soup.

I found the service to be no-nonsense, fast, & unobtrusive.  I've only tried the pastrami sandwich w/ russian dressing at one other place (Nate n' Al's) & I have to say I prefer it here (although it was a pretty close tie).  The soup was comforting on a (cold for L.A.) day.  The bread was toasted & had the perfect combination of crunch, then soft & chewy bite.  The meat was moist & juicy.  I was very happy with this pleasant meal.

I saw diners for a quick business lunch, an afternoon date, & working lunch over an Apple Mac computer.  So, this place is versatile for all needs & occasions.  I'm planning on coming back to try the other items!</Text>
